Free Talk

Reflections on "Guangzhou Like This"

— Yue Ke

A few days ago, there was an article on "Free Talk" called "Guangzhou Like This," which quoted newspapers from treacherous areas and described how shopkeepers made large statues of Zhao Gongming (God of Wealth) and Li Kui (a fictional character), embedding electric lights in their eyes to suppress the tiger sign across the street. It was truly vividly written. Naturally, the purpose was to satirize the superstitions of the people of Guangzhou.

The superstition of the Cantonese people seems to be quite considerable. Walking through the alleyways of Shanghai where people from all directions gather, if you see someone setting off firecrackers, or lighting incense and candles on the ground outside the door, nine times out of ten it's a Cantonese person. This can easily make the new party angry. However, the Cantonese are serious about their superstitions, with a certain vigor. For example, those large statues of Zhao Gongming and Li Kui probably cost at least a hundred dollars to make. The Han sought pearls, and Wu sought elephants. People from the Central Plains have always gone to Guangdong to plunder treasures, but it seems they haven't been plundered into poverty yet. They can still expend so much effort to deal with a fake tiger. Otherwise, they would simply fight to the death. This shows the seriousness of their superstition.

In reality, who in China is not superstitious? It's just that their superstitions are so unproductive that others don't pay attention. For example, if there's a tiger sign across the street, most shopkeepers will feel uncomfortable. However, in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, they probably wouldn't put in so much effort to fight it. They would just spend a copper coin to buy a strip of red paper, write "Jiang Taigong is here, all taboos are forbidden" or "Mount Tai Stone Dares to Offend," and quietly stick it up, settling down in this way. It's still superstition, but it's so small-minded, lacking vitality, and on its last legs. It won't even provide you with material for "Free Talk."

Instead of superstitious prevarication, it's better to be serious. If believing in ghosts still requires money, I approve of burying copper coins in the ground like the people of the Northern Song Dynasty did. Nowadays, burning a few paper ingots is not only deceiving others and oneself, but it's simply deceiving ghosts. Many things in China are left with only an empty name and a false appearance, precisely because of a lack of seriousness.

The superstition of the Cantonese is not worthy of emulation, but their seriousness is worth learning from and admirable.

Twilight Scenery of the Confucian Forest

— Bai Ge

Arriving in the deep autumn when red leaves are flying, and standing in the Confucian Forest at sunset, one cannot help but feel endless emotion.

This great holy land of the East has recently become desolate beyond recognition. Except for the archway at the entrance with the words "Forest of the Utmost Sage," which still majestically maintains its original appearance, everything else has changed color with the vicissitudes of human affairs. The red walls on both sides are like backboards covered with many plasters, their surfaces marred by all sorts of grandiose slogans. Some of the ancient trees along the road have fallen and decayed on the ground, losing the order of their aligned rows. But at the vast front gate, there are many protection orders issued by teachers, commanders, and directors, standing side by side like majestic guards. At this moment, a heart in awe of the sacred authority will tremble abruptly before these bayonets. Furthermore, one cannot help but feel that the sage and holy land once revered by emperors of past dynasties must now be protected by some teachers, commanders, and directors. Confucius, who traveled through various states and never sought a small position, probably would not willingly compromise himself in this way, would he?

Arriving at the second gate, one sees the withered "Zigon's Hand-Planted Scholar Tree" on the right, which can only be considered a remnant. At the same time, a group of men who look like soldiers but are not quite soldiers rush over to offer tea. It is said that they are the guardians of the forest, also descendants of Confucius, who only receive a small amount of grain from the Confucian Mansion each year to indicate their upkeep, and their livelihood depends entirely on the donations of visiting tourists. One must leave a dime or two after drinking their tea. Truly worthy of being from a family of propriety and righteousness, their hospitality is indeed not easily found elsewhere. But one cannot help but suspect that they are living off the sale of the honor of their dead ancestors, and wonder if they have accepted the teachings of "being happy in poverty and enjoying propriety in wealth." And a sense of desolation suddenly fills one's heart. Walking straight ahead, slightly uphill to the left, one reaches Confucius' tomb. Behind the tomb stands a scholar tree, covered with red leaves, that seems like and yet isn't a scholar tree, surrounded by towering ancient cypresses and pines. To the right is Zigong's mourning hut where he kept vigil, and a little further to the left is the pavilion where Emperor Qianlong and others stayed, resembling a court surrounded by officials. At this moment, another feeling of solemnity arises. Strolling forward, the sparse cemetery and shallow grassland are a place where one can both look up to the sky and roar, and wander and hum softly. Even if one does not need to visit each tomb in order, one will have a lingering thought, making one feel an indescribable mood like "Thus it passes away, like this stream!". Turning back and standing on the Zhu River Bridge to look out, another kind of world lies before one's eyes. The reeds on both banks flutter into white waves, which cannot but give rise to a feeling of detachment from the world. Going downstream, one can see red tides rolling in the endless white waves, which cannot but make one think of the famous line "fallen flowers and flowing water merging," which is precisely the short red tree drifting in the reeds. If one climbs the wall tower again and looks into the distance, it looks like a cluster of wheat stalks bearing countless spring cocoons, which will immediately make one feel endless longing for home. Looking up at the floating clouds in the sky, the hazy sunset containing the mountain gorges has long since disappeared. A remaining heart has no choice but to seek the lonely return journey through the desolate and smoky wilderness.

I think that the twilight years of some people will be about the same as this, but how many people can get such brilliant twilight years!

A Discussion on Reading Ancient Books

— Yao Ke

"What ancient books should I read?" Many friends often ask me this. Perhaps because they know that I had a study life for many years when I was young, they regard me as a "knowing old horse". In fact, although I have read ancient books for several years, I am not some "national essence scholar", and my opinions are certainly not worth a smile from "authorities". However, discussing my own experience of reading ancient books may provide a reference for "friends who want to read ancient books". I don't think reading ancient books is a necessary condition for improving new literary and artistic skills. Many people think that without a foundation in ancient books, one cannot write good new literature and art. In fact, this view has no scientific basis. Indeed, some new literary artists such as Lu Xun and Hu Shi have read ancient books, but this cannot prove that reading ancient books is a necessary condition for new literary and artistic skills. For example, Sima Qian once traveled to famous mountains and rivers, so some people insist that the goodness of the Historical Records article comes from famous mountains and rivers. But there are certainly more than just Sima Qian who have traveled to famous mountains and rivers. Why can't others write the articles of the Historical Records? From another perspective, Emperor Gaozu of the Han Dynasty came from a rogue background and had not read many ancient books at that time because they were all burned by Qin Shihuang, but his "Ode to the Great Wind" has always been regarded as a timeless masterpiece. Furthermore, many new literary writers now have not read ancient books, but they do not necessarily write new literature and art badly.

In practice, ancient books cannot provide any important help for the techniques of new literature and art - style, sentence construction, word usage, etc. Not to mention the literature and art of the pre-Qin period, just looking at the Selections of Refined Literature by Prince Zhao Ming, which was previously considered a required course, there are very few works that are useful for new literature and art. For example, the "Rhapsodies on the Two Capitals" and the "Rhapsodies on the Three Capitals" are both recognized as great. But may I ask, what use are these question-and-answer styles, the otter-sacrifice-like allusions, the rockery-building-like diction, and the couplet-like sentence construction for us? Some people say that at least reading it can increase vocabulary. That's right, there are indeed many strange and obscure words, but since one has to read "Li Shan's Annotations" to understand them, how can they naturally rush to the tip of the pen when writing? Even if they rush to it, then after the article is written, one must find a Li Jing to annotate it before the reader can understand it. This is too much trouble, and where can one find Li Shan in this day and age?

Works from the Tang and Song dynasties and later are relatively closer to our era, but they are still too far from vernacular, so they cannot make any great contribution to the techniques of new literature and art. This is not because there were no good literary and artistic works in the past that we could draw material from. It is truly because the gap between literary language and vernacular is so deep and thick that the possibility of integration is very small.

Unless one wants to do something like "reorganize the national heritage", we really do not need to read ancient books. If it is for literary and artistic cultivation, one can choose a few representative works from ancient times at will and flip through them in one's spare time, which is sufficient. If one can read more types, of course, that would be good, but it is not necessarily beneficial to the techniques of new literary and artistic writing. In addition, I think it is necessary to read a few books on literary history and history. One can roughly know about the historical changes of literature, the era of writers, and the historical background of the era. It is a pity that the Chinese publishing industry is still lagging behind in many ways. For example, there are no fine and excellent selected editions of representative works of past dynasties that meet the needs of the times, nor is there a perfect general history of our country from the perspective of historical materialism. Otherwise, scholars could save a lot of time and energy.

I do not object to reading some ancient books for the cultivation of literature and art, because this is our legacy and we are of course free to enjoy it. However, the legacy of literature and art, like the legacy of a family, also has poisonous components. People who inherit the legacy are most likely to become property-guarding people who "do not engage in production." If the descendants are unworthy, each generation will be worse than the last, and in the end, only a "bankrupt wealthy family" will remain. The drawbacks of reading ancient books often lead readers to regard ancient works as models, cultivate a mentality of imitation, and lose the courage to create. They only care about moving the outdated allusions and stale words, filling their works with dead people's words, gradually moving further and further away from living literature and art, and finally following the ancients into the tombs of the times.

In short, reading ancient books cannot make the techniques of new literature and art progress in any way, at least in my personal experience. The techniques of new literature and art must be created in the words of living people in order to have life and have a vigorous power. This is what ancient books cannot give us.

The Lying Husband

— Zhou Lengjia

On this day, the young husband's heart was uneasy, as if he had lost his soul. Although he had arrived at his own door, he forgot to raise his hand to knock.

The scene in the manager's office was constantly flashing in his mind: the manager, with a ruddy face, was crossing his legs and comfortably warming himself by the electric stove, welcoming him in with a false smile. He first engaged in some polite conversation with him, starting with the reliance he had placed on him over the past few years, and then talking about the recent universal economic downturn. Then he got to the point, saying that the store's business had also been affected by the downturn, to the point where it could not be maintained without layoffs. Because of this fact, he had to ask him to seek other employment. Then he said many words of apology before sending him out the door. At that time, he faintly heard a "clang-" sound, and the bowl that he had relied on to live for several years began to shatter.

It was from that moment that he began his uneasiness. This uneasiness transported him from the store to his own door, and never stopped.

Standing at his own door, a great anguish gripped the young husband's heart, causing him to completely lose all courage. He did not know how he would maintain his livelihood in the future, how he would maintain this lovely and happy family, and moreover, there was a major obstacle in front of him. He did not know how he would phrase things to his beloved wife.

Without even time to think, the door opened with a "crack" in his anguish, and the young wife poked her head out from behind the door. She seemed to want to come out to look at the scenery on the street, but unexpectedly saw her ghost-like husband face to face. She couldn't help but cry out in surprise.

"Why are you standing here silently?"

The young husband had to force himself to cheer up. He pretended to smile, shook his head, indicating that he was fine, and quickly took his beloved wife's hand and walked into the house. He tried his best to restrain himself, not allowing a trace of his unhappiness to leak into her eyes. He talked and laughed with her as usual, and dreamily told her many future hopes and plans. Furthermore, in order to show that he was currently happy, he even turned on the phonograph, letting the loud sound crash around the room.

But his heart was still deeply surrounded by anguish. Looking at the happy and blissful atmosphere in the house, and thinking that this would soon come to naught, and would take away the lives of both him and his beloved wife, he immediately felt as if the sofa he was sitting on was covered with steel needles, piercing him painfully.

Even lying in bed at night, the young husband's heart could not find peace. He was just tossing and turning in bed in anguish. It was not until his wife asked him in surprise why he wasn't asleep yet that he let out a few dry laughs and said:

"Darling, it's nothing, I'll be asleep right away."

The next morning, the young husband got out of bed early. The sleepless night had filled his eyes with red threads. But he still had to pretend to be very busy with his duties. He kissed his wife as usual, said goodbye to her, and closed the door gently as usual.

Walking alone on the road, a question stood in the young husband's heart: where to spend this long time? He thought of many places, and finally felt that it would be better to go to the library to read. So, he walked towards the library.

Sitting in the quiet library, a book was spread out in front of him, but he had no mood to read it. Words in black kept jumping before his eyes: "Unemployment," "Despair," "Borrowing," "Death," and the day quickly passed. (To be continued)

The Wet Nurse (5)

— Xu Zhuanpeng

The female guests drank wine, and everyone became excited. The aunt, who didn't talk much, also turned into a talkative person. She praised the child and also praised the wet nurse who raised the child. She said to the wife in front of her:

"Your wet nurse is really young, only about twenty years old, she must be ten years younger than you, right?"

"Young? Haha, the child's father picked her, he said that young people have more milk, so he chose her..."

The wife said these words reluctantly and laboriously, feeling somewhat uneasy in her heart. In front of the young wet nurse, the wife felt that she was getting old. Women are naturally fond of comparing this thing with that thing, fond of comparing themselves with others.

After the banquet, the guests chatted with each other, and suddenly the conversation turned to the wet nurse again.

"You told me a few days ago that the wet nurse was very dirty and wore ragged clothes. Today, seeing her, she is dressed neatly, young, and her character is also acceptable..." The little aunt asked the wife.

"She's dressing up now," the wife said.

"Oh, she also knows how to dress up..."

(6)

Early in the morning of the third day, the wife suddenly ordered the wet nurse:

"Go back, I've hired someone else."

"Why are you telling me to leave? Didn't you tell me to raise the child until he grows up before going home? Have I done anything wrong? Madam."

The wife never said the reason.

The female cook was also surprised. She simply didn't understand the wife's temper: "What kind of wet nurse does the wife want to choose to be satisfied? The previous wet nurse was twice as beautiful as the wife herself, and she was dismissed in a week... This one is ten years younger than the wife, but she's dismissed after only a month... The wet nurse is young, has a lot of milk, and the child is fed fat..." (The End)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Small Talk

Re-examining the "Yellow Peril"

—

The sounds of war in the world grow more urgent day by day. Due to the worsening situation in the Far East, Europe and America are constantly issuing warnings, shouting seductive and anesthetizing terms like national unity, revival, prosperity, military preparedness, etc., to incite and summon the hungry masses, urging them to endure hardship for the glory of the nation and race. How imposing are those who incite and summon, with resounding war drums and clearly displayed banners, flaunting their power!

The world, groping for a path forward in the darkness, humanity moaning in blood and gore, Mussolini, the eccentric in the eyes of the world, has again fantastically proclaimed the Yellow Peril, saying, "The Far Eastern dominance of white civilization and the fate of the Pacific depend on how China develops in the next hundred years. We can imagine that the fusion of China and Japan in the future is not impossible, but who can guarantee that their unity will not be against Europe and America?" Alas, these are truly the words of an eccentric!

Raising the banner of the Yellow Peril must have other intentions. The barbarity and violence of the Japanese are also a fact that triggers the minds of Yellow Peril proponents. We need not cover up their barbarity and violence just because of their yellow faces. However, what is the "Yellow Peril"? Will it truly become a disaster for white people? We should say a few straightforward words about this.

In Europe and America, and in our enemy country, Japan, the conservatives are all guessing that the day will soon come when the white race and the yellow race will have a struggle like in the primitive era. They guess this way, so they propagate this way, and they prepare this way. Will there be a day when the white race and the yellow race will have a struggle like in the primitive era? Looking at it from the perspective of the world economy, it becomes clear at a glance.

Today's world economy, undeniably, has reached the final stage of disintegration. The cries of hunger and the wails of displacement overflow in every corner of the world. These are not struggles between yellow and white, but struggles among people of the same color and race. But even this is not enough; they must also wield their economic, political, and military power to conquer other races – weaker nations. This is the origin of so-called racial struggles, and the fact of the weak resisting the strong arises from this.

Today, international wars are breaking out. The global changes triggered by international economic relations are like the eve of a storm, with war about to erupt. However, this is not a war of races; it is a fierce battle between imperialist countries, or between them and socialist countries or weaker nations.

Winter Plum and Nandina

— Yi Ping

After lunch, I went to the City God Temple alone. The temple is always crowded with so many people. I walked shoulder to shoulder across the Nine-Turn Bridge, and it seemed to me that coming to the City God Temple alone was too boring. I didn't want to get rich, nor did I want to live a long life. I wasn't sure about myself, so why bother to ask for help from so-called "Lords" and the like, so I angrily walked out. In front of the Small World, there were many winter plums and nandina, which seemed to interest me. I have a vase on my desk that a friend sent me from afar, but I can't afford expensive foreign flowers in the city, so I'm using it as a pen holder, which I'm really sorry for my friend's kindness in sending a goose feather from a thousand miles away; so I wrote a letter to tell him about the vase's side effects. His reply was indifferent, saying that putting it on my desk was already an unexpected honor for it, and that both flower arranging and pen holding were equally appreciating it. But thinking about it, putting flowers in a vase is as natural as putting pens in a pen holder. Today, I inadvertently discovered my beloved winter plums and nandina, and thought of how antique it would be to put them in the vase that my friend sent from afar; I even wanted to buy a small incense burner and burn three sticks of rue incense every day when I read and wrote, which would be very interesting. Thinking about it, I stopped. The seller, of course, knew the psychology of the customer. Seeing me staring blankly, he pulled down two branches of winter plum and nandina from the firewood stand, and like an artist appreciating his own work, he looked at me with his small eyes and said, "Sir, these two branches!" As he said this, he raised his hand a little higher, as if to tell me that they were even more extraordinary from a distance. In normal times, if I saw this kind of attitude, even if I went to the rice shop to buy rice to prepare dinner, I would rather tighten my belt and come back. But one cannot have hobbies; I was born loving flowers, just like Jia Baoyu was born loving rouge and powder. At that time, even if that small-eyed person put on an annoying attitude, I wouldn't be too annoyed; the winter plums and nandina in his hand were indeed lovely; I also tilted my head, pretending to appreciate them, and said, "How much?"

"Sir, you are a regular customer," he opened his mouth wide, laughing, his eyes looking even smaller, almost only seeing two piles of flesh, "Let's call it one dollar and forty cents." He stuck out his belly and brought the two branches of winter plum and nandina in front of me, his one palm facing the sky, as if a beggar begging for money on the road. But my palm couldn't stretch out; I wasn't a regular customer; if I were a regular customer, I wouldn't dare to ask "How much?" I knew myself that I only had three double-dimes in my newly made brocade crepe robe. A regular customer would naturally know that two branches of winter plum and nandina would sell for one dollar and forty cents. Would I dare to ask?

Looking at the flowers and not being able to get them, I seemed to only see that annoying attitude. I better leave quickly; putting pens in a vase isn't a crime after all; but that rough hand grabbed me, "Sir, you say." I naturally couldn't tell him that I only had sixty cents in my pocket; wouldn't that be an insult to this new robe!

"Too expensive!" I shook my head. The meaning of these two words indicated that I wasn't unable to afford it, but that the price was higher than the goods.

"Sir, you're used to buying, you say." The people around slowly gathered around. I thought they were all regular customers. People as idle as me wouldn't spend the whole afternoon wandering around the City God Temple; since I was in front of regular customers, I was asked "You say, you say" by that small-eyed person and didn't answer, wouldn't that make people laugh - not to mention the chins of the regular customers.

"Sixty cents." I said casually, confidently acting like a young master, even though my entire fortune had been declared bankrupt in this one sentence.

"Sir::" The small-eyed person just kept laughing. I thought this was an opportunity to leave, so I gracefully pushed away the two people in front of me, slowly started walking, and of course wanted to escape a little faster in my heart, but at least I should put on a good show at this time, and glanced at the second firewood stand. When the owner of that second stand - an old man with gray hair - stood up smiling, the loud "Sir" called me back. That small-eyed person stuffed the winter plum and nandina into my hand, "Sir, give whatever you want." I took it with one hand and rummaged in my pocket with the other for a long time, as if taking out sixty cents from a pile of money. The small-eyed person took the money, and unexpectedly opened his mouth and said, "Sir, Happy New Year, add a few cents if you like." Heavens! If I hadn't been wearing this new brocade crepe robe, I would have thrown the flowers and snatched back the sixty cents. Because I loved flowers, I sacrificed ten-tenths of my entire property. "New Year," what does it have to do with me, and even more so, what does it have to do with winter plums and nandina? Embarrassed to say that I didn't have another copper coin, I acted like a young master scolding a servant: "Sell if you sell, don't sell, forget it!" People are the most despicable animals after all. He silently hid the money and went to take the second deal.

Coming home, I took all the pens out of the vase, added water, and put in the winter plums and nandina, smiling quite contentedly; but I didn't dare to dream of buying any incense burners, as not having money was of course the main reason, and I was also afraid that my wife would see it and suspect that I was going to become a monk, so I wrote a letter telling my friend who sent me the vase about everything that happened, wondering what he would reply to me.

The Sound of Selling Olives

— Bin Fu

In theory, the lunar calendar should have been abolished long ago, but in reality, the people still follow the custom of using the lunar calendar. Therefore, our intellect clearly knows that it is already February, but emotionally, we cannot help but feel the end of the year, because the surrounding environment is filled with the color of "the end of the year," and it seems impossible for us to forget it.

Of all the scenes of the end of the year, none touches me more deeply than the sound of selling olives in the middle of the night. Every year at this time, the sound of selling olives appears on the streets. It has the same effect as a clock, telling us that the season has reached the cold time, and another year has passed by in a hurry.

"Olives-sell, Sandalwood-scented-olives, sell-olives!"

This sound is so mournful and poignant that it often touches my heartstrings. Especially when it is late at night, and I am coming home from outside, suddenly seeing a seller of olives carrying a dim kerosene lamp in the dark alleys, I always have to slow down my pace and listen to this moving cry; or when I am reading under the lamp, and the sound of selling olives is heard from afar, I often close my eyes and listen, listening, and often unknowingly bring tears to my eyes.

It often evokes a vague, incredible emotion in me, as if it is pity, as if it is sadness, and also like sympathy; in short, it is full of kind and loving elements. It has a great and touching power. I think that even those revelers who are drunk in pink dreams, upon hearing this sound, would not fail to be startled. Listen, so poignantly:

"Olives sell, sandalwood-scented-olives, sell-olives!"

Since I have had feeling, I have not heard a more moving song than this. The olive seller is truly a great musician, and I wish to bless him here!

The Heavy Pressure of Happiness

— Lu Zi

"People cannot be too happy; if they are too happy, happiness will crush their lives." I heard these words while I was comfortably living in happiness.

I couldn't help but laugh dumbly. Scorn climbed from my heart all the way to my face.

"Are there really people who are crushed by happiness? If so, then I should have been crushed long ago."

"Haven't you already been crushed? Alas, alas!" It seemed to echo in my ear with great regret.

"What? I've already been crushed!" I asked back in surprise.

"Yes!" Such a firm echo came.

I began to think. I felt that I was still me -- a very happy me. And there were still many people envying me? Really, my environment was very good. I was full of lightness and freedom, and there was not the slightest cumbersome weight? What's more, nothing had been crushed! This was really a rumor, and I couldn't help but feel angry.

"What heavy pressure? You liar!"

"I won't deceive you. I'm afraid it's still your own ignorance that's deceiving you, right? From the moment you were born, happiness fell on you, and your life cried. Later, the pressure of happiness increased day by day, and your life was destroyed day by day. But you will never cry again. You have become accustomed to the heavy pressure, and you have forgotten your life. The most pitiful thing in the world is a person who doesn't know that their life has been destroyed, and you are one of them."

"Oh, am I a pitiful person who doesn't know that their life has been destroyed? Then, what exactly is pressing down on me like this!"

"That is happiness, the source of your happiness -- inheritance."

"Inheritance? It's very good for me. It only gives me comfort and doesn't give me work. How can it press on me?"

"You think it's very good? That's why you've been crushed. It gives you a lot of happiness, but it hurts your life too much. The dirge is played while you are singing happily. Now you only have the empty form of life, and you no longer have the substance of life."

"No, I'm still the same as other people!"

"The same! Do you mean limbs and facial features? Then, what about your hands? Are your hands useful? Can they create anything? What about your feet? Can they walk on a smooth path? Can they blaze new trails? Can your brain even think? Can it think of things far away? Can your eyes even see? Can they see things as they truly are? But you, your whole body is just a combination of uselessness. Can this be said to be the same as other people? You, the destroyer of your life."

"It's useless, so what? As long as I have a physical form, that's enough, as long as I'm very happy, that's enough."

"But you have no life."

"Don't I feel my existence?"

"The existence of life is not based on empty form, but on substance. A life must have the power of a life; like fire having light and heat. If it has no function at all, it is just a walking corpse."

I only heard this far, and then I couldn't hear anything below. I found myself lying on the ground, completely paralyzed; I also found many heavy things pressing on my body. I could not turn over, and only had painful groans.

Who said this to me? I will be permanently confused.

"Ideal" and "Reality"

— Li Li

"Ideal is beautiful, reality is ugly!" This is the cry of young people who, after their beautiful dreams are shattered by reality, realize (?) it. This is further confirmed after reading Wen Bingjun's "Confession of an Ideal Life." Originally, young people who have not yet entered society, like the rising sun, have hearts full of red, blood boiling, spirits of striving, and thoughts of progress. To society, they build beautiful castles in the air, while at the same time harboring ambitions to reform society; when this wheel, full of sharp edges, rolls onto the rugged path of society, how many times can the tender, brittle sharp edges withstand grinding? So they break and fold, slowly becoming round and smooth, assimilating to the world. Rich in experience, smooth in dealing with people, the conditions for "being a person" are complete, and the foundation for standing in society is solid.

When the sharp edges are first injured, the beautiful castles in the air of young people are chopped down by the axe of "reality," and the ambition to reform society is stabbed by the sword of "reality." Thus, the chain of bitterness locks the hearts of young people, and when there is nowhere to place their enthusiasm and nowhere to sprinkle their hot blood, they curse "reality" on the one hand, and pursue "ideal" on the other, comparing the beautiful "ideal" with the ugly "reality," like comparing Mo Mu with Xi Shi, with a clear distinction between ugliness and beauty!

What Wen Bingjun said in "Confession of an Ideal Life": ":::decided to live the life of a recluse like those former sages:::" ":::let the bright moon accompany me, let the clear spring illuminate my heart:::" ":::as for the world, I am willing to abandon it to that group of snobs, let them meet in the conference with bombs and guns! Let them friends harm friends, relatives harm relatives:::" This said everything that young people full of indignation and jealousy want to say in their hearts, although it is not necessarily this ideal, at least the motivation is consistent, the only difference is the method!

I do not deny Wen Bingjun's words, and I have a twelve-point sympathy for Wen Bingjun, but in this chaotic world where black and white are reversed, can everything be thrown away, become a person in a peach blossom spring, maintain "purity of self" and "cultivate oneself in solitude" to reform it? I am afraid that the snobs will use bombs and guns to make it even darker, more reversed, and more chaotic.

Chuchuan Bocun said well in Symbol of Bitterness: "Iron and stone strike each other, sparking fire, torrents and rocks collide, flying out foam, producing red rainbows, similarly, two kinds of forces collide with each other, exhibiting a gorgeous kaleidoscope of life, that is, the various aspects of life." "Our life, our existence, has already fundamentally lost its meaning. Because there is the bitterness of life and the bitterness of war, people have the value of life." If Qu Yuan had been a stable official, the Lisao would not have been produced. If Sima Qian had not been subjected to palace punishment and imprisoned, how could the Historical Records have been accomplished. The mediocre life of dandy sons and the success of great men must go through thousands of hardships. These are all the results of the collision of forces. Then the youth's encounters with setbacks are excellent touchstones, so why curse, hate, and be bitter?

Young people! Don't lie in the embrace of "ideal," ignoring and forgetting "reality," but turn the beautiful "ideal" into "reality," and change the ugly "reality" into the beautiful "ideal." You must know that "reality" without "ideal" is ugly, and good "reality" is based on "ideal." The success of scientists is based on ideals. "Ideal" is the beginning of "reality," and "reality" is the end of "ideal." If you do it from beginning to end, there is no reason why things will not succeed.

Modern Celebrity Paintings and Calligraphy

— Works by Ms. Weng Wenbi from Guangdong

Inside the Classroom

— Xian

The bell, leisurely, shattered the silence of the dormitory in the early morning: in the air, depressingly, coldly, it drilled into every empty heart. Gently, I exhaled from my heart.

The few maple trees on the basketball court have shed their lush youth, revealing a haggard and sickly state; yellow leaves

Page 21

fly in patches, covering the ground. A few sparrows, lively, are looking for their food, chirping, chirping, and flapping their wings to fly east at the slightest sound. The sunlight shines down from the basketball hoop, and you can no longer feel much heat, but a gust of morning wind brings a bit of chill.

Wearing that flannel, with tweed breeches on, slowly dragging, dragging, the heavy leather shoes making a heavy sound, I moved towards that gloomy classroom.

The tired body slumped heavily into the chair, gently panting, the classroom presenting a gray and desolate gloom.

Mr. Wang, the tall and thin man with a black briefcase, jumped lightly onto the podium, loudly calling the roll, and the response was a tired, faint "Here."

Mr. Wang's clear and bright Ningbo accent spun in the air, failing to fly into everyone's ears, as if a curfew had been imposed. Every gray face showed an impatient mood, and the bodies swayed uncomfortably in the chairs, the dilapidated chairs making a burst of "creaking" sounds. Thus, the classroom slowly stirred.

A clear, beautiful, and charming figure flitted before Little Li's eyes, and then scenes of interesting memories unfolded before him.

That day on Sunday, the moment at the Grand Theater was truly perfect – smooth hands, full breasts, soft whispers, and those two vermilion lips. If the lights in the cinema hadn't come on, then taking it a step further would have been really great! Alas, what a pity, I have to wait another week, a week of life like sitting in jail. Alas, I'm so stupid...

"Bang," a fist hit the table.

People were startled and turned their heads in surprise to look at him. After that, there was a burst of laughter. He shamefully retracted that hand, still feeling a burning pain, lowered his head, and blushed in silence.

Suddenly, someone patted him on the shoulder. He awkwardly turned his head and saw a "wild monk" holding a piece of paper in his hand, stuffing it into his hand, and making a grimace at him. Looking at the paper, he saw only the following written on it:

"Daydreaming of Little Lotus, dreaming at night,

Longing for you, tears welling up,

Heart on fire when I think of hatred,

Bang, startling the classroom."

Following this was a full classroom of strange laughter, interrupting Mr. Ningbo's teaching. At this time, the sun had shone from the window lattice onto everyone's face. The sound of "beep beep" from cars also came from the road.

People slowly became lively, breaking the silent air, talking, talking about the movie at the Grand Theater, and everything at the Central Racquetball Court and the Da Hu Ballroom.

Suddenly, the bell rang clearly, striking everyone's heartstrings, perking them up. They rushed out, took the basketball to play on the playground, forgetting everything, and their faces were full of spring in autumn.

The tall, thin Mr. Wang, dejectedly, took his briefcase and slowly walked out of the classroom.

Correspondence Box

Whether a Divorce is Possible When a Husband is Kidnapped

To the Editor:

Recently, I have been pondering a matter that has caused me endless worry, confining me to a state of melancholy. Though it may seem trivial, I dare to seek assistance from you, hoping you will not hesitate to enlighten me.

In January of the 21st year of the Republic [1932], we arranged for my younger sister to marry. The other party was a middle-class farming family, with some assets, and the brother-in-law was an only son. Therefore, after the marriage, they lived in great harmony. Unexpectedly, before three months had passed, they were targeted by bandits, and he was kidnapped. It is said that they negotiated with the kidnappers several times, but due to disagreements over the ransom, no progress has been made to this day. However, rumors have spread that he has been killed. My younger sister has been widowed for nearly two years. As time passes and youth fades, how can she not be heartbroken? As her close relative, I have always wanted to speak on her behalf. However, the other party is unsophisticated, and I fear they might be unreasonable. Furthermore, I am not familiar with the law, so I have hesitated until now to intervene.

I now present four questions:

(1) Can she request a divorce? (2) If a divorce is possible, can she take her dowry with her? (3) Since the other party has no descendants, can she request alimony? (4) If she obtains alimony, can she remarry?

I earnestly request a detailed response. I eagerly await good news.

Respectfully,

Shi Zheng,

May 2nd

P.S. This letter purely reflects my younger sister's wishes and is not written under any duress.

Editor's Note: Regarding the four questions raised in the letter, we reply as follows:

(1) If the husband's death can be definitively proven, remarriage would naturally not be a problem. However, according to the letter, "no progress has been made to this day, and rumors have spread that he has been killed." While one might imagine that your sister's husband is no longer alive, there is ultimately no concrete evidence of his death. Therefore, she cannot remarry based on "presumed death." However, if this situation continues indefinitely, it would be greatly detrimental to your sister. Thus, the current Civil Code stipulates that divorce may be sought if a spouse's "whereabouts are unknown for more than three years." It appears that your sister will need to wait another year to seek a divorce.

(2) "A divorced woman, regardless of the reason for the divorce, is entitled to take with her items which are solely for her personal use, as this constitutes her separate property." (See Judgment No. 233 on divorce litigation). Therefore, this is not a problem.

(3) (4) The provisions for claiming alimony are found in Articles 1056 and 1057 of the current Civil Code. The former concerns claims for damages, while the latter concerns claims for alimony. You can consult the relevant articles yourself. However, the provision for alimony is purely intended to prevent the other party from falling into hardship. After remarriage, when someone else is responsible for her support, there would seem to be no grounds for claiming alimony. However, claiming alimony does not restrict remarriage, so she can remarry even if she obtains alimony.

Novel

The Lonely Person (8)

— Dai Ni

Xiao Xun also stood up at the same time, nodded to Jingwen's mother, and the two of them walked out of the bridal chamber.

Male and female guests surrounded them from all sides, leaving a narrow aisle in the middle. Countless pairs of eyes were looking at Kejia and Jingyi as they walked in from the outside. Qinbo was already standing beside the bride, Jingwen hurriedly pushed Xiao Xun out, and thus a pair of "jilted" protagonists enveloped a pair of "farce" protagonists.

Naturally, among the many male and female guests, those who knew the past of the four individuals, all sorts of teasing and speculation flew from the human barrier and entered the ears of each of the four.

Jingyi smiled and stayed by the side of Yeniu. Kejia played his part with a serious face. Qinbo nonchalantly showed that she was an old hand at being a bride. Xiao Xun lowered his head, his naturally loose hair dancing on top of his head. In the midst of laughter and joyful hymns, a great "farce" was completed.

Colorful streamers and confetti flew in front of everyone, pushing and shoving. As the newlyweds went into the bridal chamber, Xiao Xun slipped out like smoke. He stepped on the aisle that Jingyi and Kejia had just taken from the car and headed out the door. He felt that he was a lonely person, abandoned by the world. He regretted coming to Shanghai. Hangzhou had quiet ancient temples, deep mountains, the West Lake for boating, a small building to cultivate one's character, everything suitable for a lonely person. He even resented Kejia for deliberately flaunting his union with Jingyi in front of him. He would rather admit that he did not have the measure of a woman, that he was a weakling in the hands of women. He lowered his head and walked towards the door, shaking his naturally loose and curly hair. Suddenly, a woman's voice called his name from behind. He thought it was Jingwen and ignored it, walking straight ahead. However, the one who caught up with him side by side was Qinbo, whom he did not want to see.

"Where are you going?" she patted his shoulder, like a lover.

Xiao Xun laughed nervously, "Buying cigarettes," he answered nonchalantly.

"I have some." She took out a delicate cigarette case from her handbag, offered a cigarette to Xiao Xun, and lit it, bringing it close to Xiao Xun's lips.

"Thank you. I want to take a walk on Nanjing Road," he said, seeing that Qinbo was holding his arm, wanting him to go back in.

"Okay, let's take a walk together." This was an attitude of the girl that was completely unexpected by Xiao Xun.

The March spring breeze stirred the hearts of every young man and woman, stirred the flags of great sales, and stirred Zhu Xiao Xun's naturally loose and curly hair. The two of them walked hand in hand like a couple, without speaking, taking such short steps, along the racecourse, to Nanjing Road. Qinbo thought that Xiao Xun was buying something. After walking for a while, he still had his head lowered. Naturally, a clever girl understood everything. She forcefully pushed Xiao Xun's arm in the crook of her elbow, saying with an extremely sincere attitude:

"Xiao Xun, are you still angry with me?" Her pupils seemed to shrink, and her brows were locked tightly.

"Qinbo, why do you still bring up such things?" He laughed nervously, shaking his naturally loose and curly hair.

"You should forgive me, Li Shaojie is not a person!" Her high heels heavily hit the cement.

Reader, I will tell you an amazing piece of evidence that the earth is round. Xiao Xun and Qinbo kept walking forward, but they arrived in front of the hotel; as for whether they had turned a corner, I did not pay attention.

However, there was someone in front of the hotel who noticed - it was Jingwen. After a flurry of commotion in the temporary bridal chamber, they discovered that a pair of male and female attendants were missing. There was the sign of that naturally loose and curly hair. A waiter told them that he had walked out with a female guest. Jingwen rushed to the front of the door and saw the two of them, but they themselves did not know that they had circled the "earth" once.

"Little brother:" she shouted with a smile.

Of course, a clever man also understands everything. Xiao Xun threw off Qinbo's arm and ran forward a few steps.

"Haven't seen Shanghai for three months," everything has changed! He shook his naturally loose and curly hair.

Film Special

Mr. Dareos's Prediction: Hollywood's Trends This Year (Part 1)

— Bing Jian

Garbo will leave the film industry forever

Fairbanks will return to Hollywood

We have seen many predictions about world affairs this year, but there seem to be few about the film industry.

The American film magazine "Modern Screen" published an article in its February issue about Hollywood's predictions. The predictor is the well-known Mr. Dareos in Hollywood. Mr. Dareos also made the same predictions at the beginning of last year, predicting 68 things. Of these 68 things, 48 were correct, i.e., 70%; 8 were wrong, i.e., 11%; and 12 had no results, accounting for 17%. Although his predictions are not 100% accurate, the 70% accuracy rate is quite remarkable. The following is a selection of the more important ones:

First, let's talk about Mae West, who was the most popular last year. Mr. Dareos predicted that Mae West would still live a single life in 1934. Although she will continue to be romantic this year, she will eventually retain the title of Miss Mae West. In the film industry, her position will be further consolidated and become a red star. However, in terms of finances, she will generally lose some.

Secondly, let's talk about Joan Crawford. Crawford's achievements this year can be said to have reached its peak. But after this, the better the year, the more she will fail. In terms of love, she may think she is satisfied, but she will never find true love. It will not be until 1935 that she can remarry.

Speaking of Garbo, it's simply bad luck. She will not be able to show any more amazing results in the future. If she does not give up her film career in 1934, then she will retire at the latest in 1935, and it will be her last and forever retirement. She will return to her hometown in Sweden.

Jenny Gaynor, this cute little bird, is going to be a bride again this year. Even if she cannot get married this year, she will definitely announce her engagement before the end of the year. The future husband will be older than her and will be a divorced man. She will give birth to a little baby in 1935. She will have two more years of good luck in the film industry. After this, she should retire.

So what about Clark Gable? Gable will definitely continue to get along with her current husband, Rex Bell. She will give birth to a son this year. This child will definitely become famous in the future. But from which aspect--screen, stage, or other?--it is not yet known.

Jean Harlow is also unlucky this year. There will be countless rumors slandering her this year. In Mr. Dareos's crystal ball, all the constellations are standing in opposition to Harlow. If she can get through this difficulty, then she will have two years of good luck in the future.

Kathleen Hepburn had good luck last year. She is not very popular this year. Although she will encounter many setbacks this year, she will eventually be able to climb up. She will feel a great pain in her personal life this year. (To be continued)

Audience Opinions

Review of "The Youth of Blood"

— Green Intentions

"The Youth of Blood" is a work by Tianyi Company that is completely opposite in personality and tone to "The Fire of Youth." Director Tang Jie is the first work to enter Tianyi Company, and it is much more advanced in technique than the "Mother and Child" directed by Mingxing. The whole play uses a heavy and slow tone, which can better increase the tragedy (although The Youth of Blood is not a complete tragedy) the achievement! There are also small cleverness, such as using cigarette ashes to show the father's advanced thoughts: using Ke Jianzi overturning the rice bucket to symbolize the unemployment of Ke Jian's father and son, etc. The application of symbolism is the same method as in "Drifting", which is a pity to become the old tune of Tianyi Company.

Tianyi Company's works also have a common shortcoming, that is, there are several sections of funny interspersed in each work! In "The Fire of Youth" it is the servant's strange face; now in "The Youth of Blood" it is the neighbor's movements and the bill collector's expression, which can most destroy the serious atmosphere of the plot. The producers set this up in order to welcome the general low-level taste, we really dare not agree. You must know that the funny interspersion can still be used slightly in a relaxed comedy, but in a bitter mood, it is greatly weakened the dramatic power when applied.

"The Youth of Blood" also dragged a big tail. This tail completely destroyed the tragic mood, and gave the audience an impression: the traitor was finally arrested - although this is very popular, the sympathy for the death of Ke Jian's parents has disappeared a lot! I think if the ending is changed to Ke Jian's police officer going to the cargo agency, he will be imprisoned for false accusations due to lack of evidence, then the structure will be completed as a complete tragedy, and the audience will strengthen their hatred for the traitor, so isn't it better?

Review of "Life"

— 克洛

In terms of technique, "Life" can be said to surpass all domestic films. The clear and beautiful photography, the reasonable and symmetrical setting, the flexible rotation of the lens, and the competent efforts of the actors are all impeccable and worthy of praise; especially this time Fei Mu used that novel directing technique - a slow melody, which made every audience member feel a heavy pressure in their hearts, and increased the power of the tragedy.

However, in terms of consciousness, I think it is not only not as good as "Spring Silkworms" and "Salt Tide", but has a great retrogression! Its central consciousness is the struggle between "good" and "evil", and to make people turn "evil" into "good", the power of education must be used. In this way, it has three shortcomings:

(1) There is no effort to describe the causes of "evil";

(2) It is simply a fantasy to want to use the power of education to make people turn "evil" into "good". Before the economic structure of the current society is improved, the so-called education is used by the privileged class as a tool to cultivate slaves. Not only can it not make people turn "evil" into "good", or it will produce a lot of evil people!

(3) Put all hope in the "future" and abandon the "reality"!

However, from a humanitarian point of view, this film has a lot of power to make people shed two tears of sympathy!

My Opinion on "Life"

— 越熙

The performance of "Life", although I dare not say that it has broken through all the achievements of Chinese films and has risen to the world status, but it is indeed a rare and praiseworthy film, especially from the technical point of view.

For example, using "ironing" to symbolize "life's tempering" is the playwright's extremely clever place. Of course, this is not easy to understand for people without artistic cultivation; but it is extremely unreasonable and stupid to deliberately lower the standards of art in order to cater to the psychology of low-level audiences. The film itself has the mission of improving the audience's artistic understanding.

For example, the picture shows the train proceeding, followed by Lin Ruan meeting. This saves a lot of unnecessary pictures, which is very commendable. Others, such as Fei Boqing drawing a gun and turning to prison, etc., are all very economical methods of the director, which are rare in Chinese films.

The clarity of light and the beauty of the picture are undoubtedly impeccable and satisfactory.

In terms of actors, I think Ruan Lingyu played the most realistic, the most effort, the most successful, and the most able to give the audience a deep impression. Fei Boqing's face is cunning, which is in line with the plot, and it is also considered a success. Zheng Junli failed to give the audience a deep impression, and we should forgive him for having too few opportunities to act. The rest of the actors can do their job well. In addition, our little star-Li Keng, who occupies the first seat of child actors-seems to have performed less well in this than in the past "City Night" and "Humanity" (omitted below)

Review of "Life"

— Xu Menggan

The current society is a deformed monster of all evils. Life is a portrayal and narration of a corner of this deformed society.

The protagonists in "Life"; one is a prostitute who has been transformed from a wild child and a maid, one is an elementary school teacher who is unwilling to be buried in chalk dust, and one is his wife who serves in a nursery. Under such circumstances, an unsurpassed and tragic tragedy was staged.

Regarding the director's technique, Fei Mu has made more progress than in "City Night". Although he does not explain everything about the characters in the play, he can use the kisses of the characters in the play to express them, and he can also narrate them in an orderly manner, which is his unique style.

Regarding the expressions of the actors. Then Wan Lingyu and Lin Chuchu are the most moving, Li Jian's innocence, Zheng Junli's handsome, are all commendable, and other actors can also do their best. As for photography, setting and other aspects, they are more advanced than before.

In short: in the embryonic stage of domestic films, "Life" is an ultra-special work. At the same time, we can also see that the Chinese film industry is making rapid progress, and is closely following foreign films.

The Shanghai Cinema Screens "The Lady Hunter"

A comedy full of pleasant atmosphere

"The Lady Hunter" Facing The Music is a British musical comedy. The protagonist, Stan Rubio, is the younger brother of Lubelin, the funny waiter in "Xuan Palace Romance." His reputation in the European film industry is not inferior to that of Hollywood's Schiffrin. This arrogant child is completely composed of beautiful music, pleasant songs, and then the technology of film. Therefore, not only is the whole film funny and interesting; the songs included in it are very famous. In the "Faust", which has the longest history in the drama world, the song "Jewel Song" has also been moved to the film. This is very worthy of attention. And the actress who plays the female role is also a famous singer in Europe. The most gratifying thing is that under the director's clear description, each actor can grasp the unique personality of each character in the play. It is not easy for a comedy to have such good results. This film has been scheduled to be screened at the Great Shanghai Grand Theater starting today (7th).

Film Novel

Christina Queen Chrina (6)

— Hu Chen

Outside the inn, there was already the sound of people and horses making noise. She knew that the Spanish team had arrived. She watched them run into the inn one by one. She heard the imperial envoy ask the innkeeper for a room. She saw the innkeeper shaking his shoulders and apologizing repeatedly. The innkeeper looked at Christina, as if saying that she was the reason why he had no room to sleep in. So the imperial envoy quickly ran up to her. He took off his hat and bowed deeply. He said, "Sir, I have not had the pleasure of knowing you before, and I have been very rude. Now I am here to apologize." Christina smiled and said, "Sir, you don't need to be so humble. I earned that pound very happily." The young man said again, "Sir, this really makes me feel ashamed." Christina said, "Sir, there is no reason for that. I blame myself for wearing clothes that are too unlike yours." She looked at the rough sheepskin jacket she was wearing, "Isn't it the appearance of clothes that shows identity when we meet for the first time?" The man looked at her and said, "Sir, I hope you will allow me to get to know you better. Can you give me the honor of inviting you to dinner?" Christina said, "Having dinner together is possible, as long as you allow me to be the host. You are a guest from afar, and I must do my best to be a good host. I invite you to dinner today, will you give me the pleasure? And I have a deep concern for your country from which you came." The young imperial envoy declined on the one hand, and on the other hand, he asked her in surprise, "Do you know Spain?" Christina smiled and said, "I know Spain very well. I also want to learn some recent news from you. Does Floraskis have any new works of art? What has Gartelton been doing in Madrid recently?"

He was obviously surprised. He asked, "When were you last in Spain?" Christina said, "I have never been there, but I often think about it." The Spanish man's black eyes shone with light and said, "How strange! I am so happy to meet you, you will never know... Innkeeper!" The innkeeper came. The young man ordered, "Prepare the best dinner for this gentleman tonight." He then turned back to Christina and said, "Have you ever had homesickness?" Christina said apologetically, "I have never left the borders of Sweden." The young man said, "Then you will not know the taste of that loss. It is a kind of nostalgic mourning." Christina said slowly, "Do you know that even a person who has never been to a place can feel homesick?" This made him even more surprised. He said, "That is of course possible. This is the second time I have been disrespectful to you. You are a rare young man. Come," he took her hand and walked to the dining table.

On the other side, the innkeeper and his wife were discussing: the young man gave twenty taels, but the foreigner promised to give thirty taels, as long as he had a bed to sleep in. Now he watched Christina and the foreign young man talking very happily, so he came up. He smiled slyly without opening his mouth first and said, "I think you two gentlemen are very good friends. If possible, we can think of a way so that this gentleman can also have a place to stay." He said, pointing to the Spanish imperial envoy. (To be continued)
